Summary 173:
Rights of passengers in bus and coach transport: non-discrimination and assistance in case of accidents
Rules of conduct for disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility in the transport sector
Rights for disabled passengers in the transportation sector
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 181/2011 on the rights of passengers of buses and coaches
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure a high level of protection for passengers who travel by bus or coach in the European Union (EU).
It lays down rules for non-discrimination and assistance during their journey.
It amends Regulation (EC) No 2006/2004.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
passengers and, as a minimum, persons whom the passenger had, or would have had, a legal duty to maintain and who are the weaker party to the transport contract, as well as to persons who are not covered by such a contract.
Passengers are entitled to compensation in accordance with applicable national law in the event of death or personal injury or loss of or damage to luggage arising out of the use of the bus and/or coach, except for reasons which are justified on the grounds of safety or of the design of the vehicle or infrastructure.
Assistance
Disabled passengers and persons who have reduced mobility must receive free of charge:
first aid, accommodation, food, clothes and transport;
medical assistance, including first aid, where necessary, first aid and accommodation;
food, clothing and transport.
in addition to compensation, passengers should, in addition to assistance, be entitled to assistance with regard to their immediate practical needs following an accident.
EU Member States must notify the European Commission of any new or refurbished buses or coaches with a disability or reduced mobility.
Member States must also notify the Commission of all new buses, refurbished coaches and new buses with a reduced mobility requirement and of any refurbishment of existing ones.
The Commission must inform Member States of any changes to the rules on the right of access to assistance for disabled people.
In addition, Member States are required to ensure that:
the Commission publishes a report every 5 years on the implementation of the regulation and on the measures taken by Member States to improve the protection of passengers’ rights in the field of public transport. The report must include a summary of the Commission’s findings and recommendations.
Commission Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/852 amends the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?

KEY TERMS

* Reduced mobility: a disability caused by reduced mobility due to age or other factors, such as age, disability, reduced mobility or disability.

Summary 174:
Statistics on aquaculture
Statistical data on the EU’s fisheries sector
Statistics on the European Aquaculture sector
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 762/2008 on the submission by EU countries of statistics on aquatic production
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It establishes a common legal framework for the collection and submission of EU statistics on the production of aquacultural products in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation requires EU countries to submit to the European Commission statistics on:
aquaculture production;
the volume of production; and
the value of production.
EU Member States must submit annual data to the Commission on the volume and value of the production in freshwater and salt waters on their territory.
The Commission may adopt technical changes to the annexes to this regulation. These changes must conform with the principles of impartiality, reliability, relevance, cost-effectiveness, statistical confidentiality and transparency.
Annexes to the regulation specify the purpose of the data collection and the methods used for collecting the data. The annexes also provide information on the structure of the sector and on the technologies employed to ensure an environmentally sound industry.
Requirements for Member States
Member States must:
ensure that the data are collected in accordance with the rules laid down in Regulation (EU) No 322/97 on Community Statistics (see summary);
provide the Commission with a report on the year in which the data were collected;
provides a description of the methods and methods used to collect the data;
give the Commission an estimate of the volume, value and volume of the total production of the products produced in their territory;
report the results of the statistical analysis to the Council of the EU on the basis of the information provided by the Member States.
Report the Commission to the EU Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Standing Committee for Agricultural Statistics on the quality of the statistics collected. The Commission must submit the report to the Parliament and the Council within 3 years of the date of entry into force of the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULUMENT APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE?
It entered into force on 13 August 2008.
BACKGROUND
The increased contribution to the Union's total fisheries production requires a wider range of data for a rational development and management of this sector within the Common Fisheries Policy. This regulation provides a reference framework for statistics in the field of fisheries.
For more information, see:
Aquaculture statistics (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* EU Member States:
collecting and transmitting statistics on all the aquatic activities conducted in freshwater or salt water on their territories.
* Data collection: the collection of annual data by Member States on the total volume of aquatic production and the value of aquatic products produced.

Summary 175:
North-East Atlantic fisheries: control and enforcement — North-east Atlantic fisheries (Convention on future multilateral cooperation in the North-Atlantic fisheries) (Regulation (EU) No 1236/2010)
North–East Atlantic Fisheries Commission (NEAFC) — North–West Atlantic Fisheries Scheme
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 81/608/EEC on the signing, on behalf of the European Union (EU), of the Convention on Future Multilateral Cooperation on the rational conservation and management of fishery resources in the Area defined by the Convention (the Convention Area) (Decision (EC) No 43/2009 on the fishing opportunities and associated conditions for certain fish stocks and groups of fish stocks, applicable in EU waters and, for EU vessels, in waters where catch limitations are required.
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND THE DECISION?
The regulation sets out the rules applicable to fishing vessels operating in the waters of the convention area which lie beyond the waters under the fisheries jurisdiction of the contracting parties (known as the North–west Atlantic Fisheries Convention).
The decision repeals and repeals Council Regulation No 2791/1999.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The convention applies to vessels flying the flag of contracting parties and fishing vessels flying their flag in the area covered by the convention. It does not apply to non-contracting parties.
EU countries must control access to waters and resources and control activities outside EU waters carried out by vessels operating under their flag.
Inspectors are authorised to fish in the Convention Area to undertake monitoring and surveillance, as well as to carry out inspection and inspection at sea.
Member States must designate inspectors to the scheme to undertake inspections and surveillance and to provide adequate resources for inspection. Member States must notify the European Commission and the Commission with detailed rules on the authorisation and authorisation of fishing vessels.
The Commission must notify Member States of any changes to the list of vessels that have been confirmed to have engaged in illegal, unreported and unregulated fishing activities. The Commission must also notify the Commission of any amendments to the lists of vessels which are subject to incorporation into EU law.
Enforcement
Member states must take all necessary measures to ensure compliance with the convention and the rules of the common fisheries policy, including:
implementing the inspection and surveillance procedures and infringement procedures laid down in the convention;
ensuring that vessels are notified of any acts of transshipment of frozen fish which have not been verified to be legal by the port state of a contracting party other than that port state;
taking all appropriate measures to prevent the entry into force of any fishing vessels that are suspected of engaging in illegal fishing activities outside the convention areas.
Implementation of the regulation
Each year, Member States submit a report to the Commission on the implementation of this regulation. The report must include:
the number of vessels covered by this regulation;
the total number of catches and the number of tonnes of fish caught during the previous year;
a description of the number and type of fishing gear and equipment used;
details of the types of fishing equipment used.
If a vessel is found to be engaged in fishing activities that are contrary to the convention, the Commission must inform the other contracting parties of the vessel’s registration, registration, authorisation or authorisation, and of the measures taken to prevent it from continuing to engage in such activities.
National authorities must inform each other of any vessel that is suspected of being involved in illegal activities. Member states must also inform the Commission if they consider that a vessel has been found to have been involved in an illegal fishing activity.
Commission Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/852 amends the regulation to:
ensure that the Commission adopts a list of the vessels subject to the regulation and the measures to be taken in respect of these vessels;
establish a system of inspections and inspections at sea;
introduce a system for the notification and notification of changes in the rules and authorisations of authorisations for fishing vessels in accordance with the regulation.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE

Summary 176:
EU Ecolabel — rules on the environmental performance of products (e.g. the EU Ecolabel)
European Union (EU) ecolabel – rules on environmental performance
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 66/2010 on the European Union’s eco-label award scheme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to promote products with a reduced environmental impact during their entire life cycle and to provide consumers with accurate, non-deceptive, science-based information about the environmental impact of products.
It sets out the criteria and procedures for the award of the EU ecolabels.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
food and feed products, as well as unprocessed agricultural products that lie within the scope of Regulation (EC), No 834/2007 on organic production and labelling of organic products;
organic products certified as organic;
energy-related products, such as biofuels and energy-efficient appliances;
non-food products, which are subject to the requirements of Directive 2009/125/EC on ecodesign requirements for energy related products (see summary).
It does not apply to products that are classified as organic.
Ecolabel criteria
The criteria for the EU eco-labelling award scheme are based on the best environmental performance achieved by products on the EU market. These criteria must be market oriented and limited to the most significant environmental impacts of products during their whole life cycle. They must be based on scientific evidence, taking into account the latest technological developments.
.
The European Commission may submit proposals to any interested party to develop or revise the criteria provided that common procedural rules are followed and that the development or revision of the criteria is coordinated with the European Environment Protection Agency (EPAA).
The Commission may adopt a proposal for the development of new criteria. It must submit the proposal to the EPAA within 6 months of receiving the proposal. The EPAA may, in particular, examine the suitability of the new criteria for use in order to adapt them to the latest scientific and technological developments in the field of environmental labelling.
If the Commission adopts a proposal, it must submit it to the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee of the Regions. The proposal must contain the following information:
the nature of the product and its environmental performance;
a description of the products and the conditions for their use;
the conditions for the use of the European Ecolabilisation Programme (EPC) and the rules for the verification of compliance with the EPC;
details of the procedure for the implementation of the regulation and for the revision of its criteria. The Commission must submit a report to the Parliament and the Council every 6 months on the application of the Regulation and the results of the verification procedure. The report must include information on the number of products that have been certified as Ecolabs and the criteria that have applied for the Ecolalisation Programme.
In addition, the Commission must publish a report every 6 years on the progress made in the development and revision of EU EColabel criteria. This report must be submitted to the EU Parliament and to the Council on the basis of the information it has received.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
    Ебанка бака  бългальна гаралка, блакованска (Ecolabela) is the name of a voluntary European Union (European Commission) award scheme for products which have a high level of environmental performance. It is part of the sustainable consumption and production policy (Sustainable Consumption and Production Policy) which aims at reducing the negative impact of consumption on the environment, health, climate and natural resources.
BACKGROUND
The EU eco label award scheme was established in 2000. It was amended in 2000 to increase its effectiveness and streamline its operation.
For more information, see:
European Commission eColabel (European Agency for Safety and Health at Work).
KEY TERMS
* Ecolabus: a European Union eco label.
* Environmental performance: a product that has a low environmental impact throughout its life cycle, i.e. during its production, processing, storage, transport, storage and disposal.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Банъанна  хлабказа блхалика: a quality assurance system for products. It aims to ensure that products which meet certain criteria are recognised as having a high environmental performance and that consumers can make informed choices about the products they buy and use.

Summary 177:
Supplementary protection certificate for medicinal products
Supplementary Protection Certificate
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 469/2009 — supplementary protection certificate
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It codifies and repeals Council Regulation (EEC) 1768/92 concerning the creation of a supplementary patent certificate for medicines.
It aims to ensure that medicinal products covered by a patent are protected for a maximum of 15 years.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to any substance or combination of substances presented for treating or preventing disease in human beings or animals and any substance which may be administered to humans or animals with a view to making a medical diagnosis or to restoring, correcting or modifying physiological functions in humans or in animals.
Beneficiaries of the regulation include:
the holder of a national or European patent relating to a medicinal product for which marketing authorisation has been granted;
the authorisation to place the medicinal product on the market in the European Union (EU).
The duration of the protection granted by the certificate must be such as to provide adequate effective protection. For this purpose, the certificate cannot be granted for a period exceeding five years. The protection granted should furthermore be strictly confined to the product which obtained authorisation as an authorised medicinal product.
Expiry of the certificate
The certificate is valid for 15 years from the date on which it is granted. It may be renewed for an additional period of 5 years if a patent term has already expired or if the holder of the patent applies for a patent extension.
has already been extended under a specific national law.
Provision of extension of the duration of protection
In the case of a patent, the extension of protection may be extended for a further period of 10 years. However, the duration may not exceed 5 years in the case where the patent term had already expired.
In addition, the authorisation granted by an EU country to place on the EU market must be renewed at least once every 5 years. This period may not be less than the maximum period of effective protection granted under the patent.
EU countries may grant a certificate for a product which is subject to a prior authorisation and which has not yet been placed on the European market. The authorisation must be valid for at least 5 years after the application for authorisation is filed.
The authorisation may be granted only to products which have been granted authorisation for the purpose of marketing.
Application for a certificate
An application may be made to the European Patent Office (EPO) or the European Medicines Agency (EMAA) for the granting of a certificate. The application must be accompanied by a copy of the original patent application.
If the EPO decides to grant the certificate, it must inform the European Commission of the reasons for its decision. The Commission may adopt delegated acts to amend the regulation in the light of the Commission’s proposal.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 16 June 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Patent: a patent which protects a product as a process, a process or a product designated by its holder and which is designated as a product for use in the EU.
* Medicinal product: any substance, combination or active ingredient, which is intended to treat or prevent disease or to restore or modify physiological functions.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егранска барка  болода   ганка, борака (OJ L 152, 16.6.2009, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, No 468/1992 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 178:
Convention on jurisdiction and the recognition and enforcement of judgments in civil and commercial matters (Lugano Convention)
Convention of the High Contracting Parties to the Lugano Convention
SUMMARY OF:
Council Regulation (EC) No 44/2001 — jurisdiction and recognition and enforceability of judgments — Civil and Commercial matters
Decision (EU) 2017/852 on the conclusion of the Convention on Jurisdiction and the Recognition and Enforcement of Judgments in Civil & Commercial Matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND THE CONVENTION?
The regulation establishes the jurisdiction of the courts of the countries that are parties to the convention. The convention sets out the rules of jurisdiction applicable to the courts in those countries.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The convention applies to:
the status or legal capacity of natural persons, rights in property arising out of a matrimonial relationship, wills and succession;
bankruptcy proceedings relating to the winding-up of insolvent companies or other legal persons, judicial arrangements, compositions and analogous proceedings;
social security;
arbitration.
It does not apply to revenue, customs or administrative matters.
Jurisdiction
A person domiciled in a country bound by the convention may be sued in the court of another country by virtue of the rules set out in Annex I of this Convention.
If the defendant is not a national of the country in which is bound by this Convention, the law of that country is governed by that country’s law. However, persons who are not nationals of the state in which the defendant lives may, subject to the rules applicable to nationals of that state, sue in its courts.
Recognition and enforcement
The courts of each EU country that is a contracting party to this convention must recognise and enforce judgments, authentic instruments and court settlements issued by another EU country.
Where a judgment is recognised and enforced in another country, it must be enforced in the country where the judgment was delivered.
A judgment may only be recognised in that country if it is authentic and has been delivered in the territory of the EU country which issued it.
In the case of authentic instruments, the judgment may be recognised only if it has been issued by the competent court of a country which is a party to the Convention. If it is issued by a court in a non-EU country, the court in which it was issued must recognise it and enforce it. If the judgment is not authentic, it may not be enforceable in that state.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Convention entered into force on 1 July 2009.
BACKGROUND
   
 
The Lugano convention was amended by the Accession Conventions under the successive enlargements of the Union.
For more information, see:
Judgment and recognition of judgments (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Resolution (EC, Euratom) No 852/2009 of 27 September 2008 on the interpretation of Council Regulations (EC).
Council Decision (EU), Euratom and the European Free Trade Association (Euratom) of 22 December 2009 on the application of the convention of the 1968 Brussels Convention on jurisdiction (OJ L 147, 10.6.2009, pp. 5-8)
Council Convention of 16 September 1988 on jurisdiction* and the enforcement* of judgments* in civil & commercial matters, as amended by Articles 22 and 23 of the accession convention.
last update 04.02.2021
